# Question Bank — Sec 1 Express Mathematics
**Total:** 2101 MCQs across 14 topics

## Topic 1: Primes, HCF & LCM
*Prime factorisation, square/cube roots, HCF and LCM* — 150 questions

### PRIME NUMBERS (Q1–25)

1. Which of the following is a prime number?
   - A) 9 | B) 15 | **C) 17** | D) 21
   - *17 has exactly two factors: 1 and 17. It is prime. 9 = 3×3, 15 = 3×5, 21 = 3×7 are all composite.*

2. Which of the following is NOT a prime number?
   - A) 2 | B) 3 | **C) 9** | D) 11
   - *9 = 3 × 3, so it has factors other than 1 and itself. It is not prime.*

3. How many prime numbers are there between 1 and 10?
   - A) 3 | **B) 4** | C) 5 | D) 6
   - *Primes between 1 and 10: 2, 3, 5, 7 — that's 4 primes.*

4. Which is the only even prime number?
   - A) 1 | **B) 2** | C) 4 | D) 6
   - *2 is the only even prime. All other even numbers are divisible by 2 and hence composite.*

5. Is 1 a prime number?
   - A) Yes, it has one factor | **B) No, primes need exactly two factors** | C) Yes, because it is odd | D) No, it is even
   - *1 has only one factor (itself). A prime must have exactly two distinct factors: 1 and itself. So 1 is not prime.*

6. Which of the following is prime?
   - A) 27 | B) 33 | **C) 37** | D) 39
   - *37 is prime — not divisible by 2, 3, or any prime up to √37 ≈ 6.1. The others: 27 = 3³, 33 = 3×11, 39 = 3×13.*

7. How many prime numbers are between 20 and 30?
   - A) 1 | **B) 2** | C) 3 | D) 4
   - *Primes between 20 and 30: 23 and 29 — that's 2.*

8. Which list contains only prime numbers?
   - A) 2, 4, 6 | B) 3, 9, 15 | **C) 2, 3, 5, 7** | D) 5, 10, 15
   - *2, 3, 5, 7 are all prime. The others contain composites (4, 6, 9, 10, etc.).*

9. Is 51 prime?
   - A) Yes | **B) No, 51 = 3 × 17** | C) No, 51 = 7 × 7 | D) No, 51 = 3 × 13
   - *51 = 3 × 17. Since it has factors other than 1 and 51, it is composite.*

10. What is the largest prime number less than 20?
   - A) 17 | B) 18 | **C) 19** | D) 16
   - *19 is prime (not divisible by 2, 3, or any prime ≤ √19 ≈ 4.4). 18 = 2×9, 17 is also prime but smaller.*

11. Which of the following is a prime number?
   - A) 49 | B) 51 | **C) 53** | D) 55
   - *53 is prime. 49 = 7², 51 = 3×17, 55 = 5×11.*

12. How many factors does a prime number have?
   - A) 1 | **B) 2** | C) 3 | D) More than 3
   - *By definition, a prime number has exactly 2 factors: 1 and itself.*

13. Which of these is NOT prime?
   - A) 13 | B) 17 | C) 19 | **D) 21**
   - *21 = 3 × 7. It has 4 factors, so it is composite.*

14. Is 2 prime?
   - A) No, it is even so composite | **B) Yes, it has exactly two factors** | C) No, it has three factors | D) Yes, all even numbers are prime
   - *2 is prime. It has exactly two factors: 1 and 2. It's the only even prime.*

15. What is the smallest prime number greater than 10?
   - **A) 11** | B) 12 | C) 13 | D) 15
   - *11 is prime (only factors are 1 and 11). 12 = 2²×3, 13 is also prime but larger than 11.*

16. Which set of numbers are all prime?
   - A) 11, 13, 15, 17 | **B) 11, 13, 17, 19** | C) 13, 15, 17, 19 | D) 11, 14, 17, 19
   - *11, 13, 17, 19 are all prime. 15 = 3×5 and 14 = 2×7 are composite.*

17. How many prime numbers are between 10 and 20?
   - A) 3 | **B) 4** | C) 5 | D) 6
   - *Primes between 10 and 20: 11, 13, 17, 19 — that's 4.*

18. Which of the following is composite?
   - A) 7 | B) 11 | C) 23 | **D) 25**
   - *25 = 5 × 5. It has factors 1, 5, 25 so it is composite.*

19. Is 97 prime?
   - **A) Yes** | B) No, 97 = 7 × 13 | C) No, 97 = 9 × 11 | D) No, 97 = 3 × 31
   - *97 is prime. It is not divisible by 2, 3, 5, 7 (primes up to √97 ≈ 9.8).*

20. What is the sum of the first three prime numbers?
   - A) 6 | B) 8 | **C) 10** | D) 12
   - *First three primes are 2, 3, 5. Their sum is 2 + 3 + 5 = 10.*

21. Which prime is between 40 and 50?
   - A) 41 and 43 | B) 41 and 47 | C) 43 and 47 | **D) 41, 43 and 47**
   - *Primes between 40 and 50: 41, 43, 47. (45 = 3²×5, 49 = 7²)*

22. Is 91 prime?
   - A) Yes | **B) No, 91 = 7 × 13** | C) No, 91 = 9 × 10 | D) No, 91 = 11 × 8
   - *91 = 7 × 13. It is composite. A common trick question!*

23. Which of these has exactly 2 factors?
   - A) 6 | B) 8 | **C) 11** | D) 15
   - *11 has exactly 2 factors: 1 and 11. It is prime. 6, 8, 15 each have more than 2 factors.*

24. The number 1 is:
   - A) Prime | B) Composite | **C) Neither prime nor composite** | D) Both prime and composite
   - *1 is neither prime (needs exactly 2 factors) nor composite (composites have more than 2 factors). 1 is in its own category.*

25. How many prime numbers are between 50 and 60?
   - A) 0 | B) 1 | **C) 2** | D) 3
   - *Primes between 50 and 60: 53 and 59. That's 2.*

### PRIME FACTORISATION (Q26–60)

26. Express 12 as a product of prime factors.
   - A) 2 × 6 | **B) 2² × 3** | C) 3 × 4 | D) 2 × 3²
   - *12 = 2 × 2 × 3 = 2² × 3.*

27. Express 18 as a product of prime factors.
   - A) 2 × 9 | **B) 2 × 3²** | C) 3 × 6 | D) 2² × 3
   - *18 = 2 × 9 = 2 × 3 × 3 = 2 × 3².*

28. Express 36 as a product of prime factors.
   - A) 2² × 9 | B) 4 × 9 | **C) 2² × 3²** | D) 6²
   - *36 = 4 × 9 = 2² × 3².*

29. Express 24 as a product of prime factors.
   - **A) 2³ × 3** | B) 2² × 6 | C) 4 × 6 | D) 2 × 12
   - *24 = 2 × 12 = 2 × 4 × 3 = 2³ × 3.*

30. Express 30 as a product of prime factors.
   - A) 2 × 15 | B) 5 × 6 | **C) 2 × 3 × 5** | D) 2² × 5
   - *30 = 2 × 15 = 2 × 3 × 5. All three factors are prime.*

31. Express 45 as a product of prime factors.
   - A) 5 × 9 | **B) 3² × 5** | C) 3 × 15 | D) 5² × 3
   - *45 = 9 × 5 = 3² × 5.*

32. Express 60 as a product of prime factors.
   - **A) 2² × 3 × 5** | B) 4 × 15 | C) 2 × 3 × 10 | D) 2³ × 5
   - *60 = 4 × 15 = 2² × 3 × 5.*

33. Express 72 as a product of prime factors.
   - A) 8 × 9 | **B) 2³ × 3²** | C) 2² × 18 | D) 2 × 36
   - *72 = 8 × 9 = 2³ × 3².*

34. Express 48 as a product of prime factors.
   - **A) 2⁴ × 3** | B) 2³ × 6 | C) 4 × 12 | D) 2² × 12
   - *48 = 16 × 3 = 2⁴ × 3.*

35. Express 100 as a product of prime factors.
   - A) 4 × 25 | B) 10² | **C) 2² × 5²** | D) 2 × 50
   - *100 = 4 × 25 = 2² × 5².*

36. Express 84 as a product of prime factors.
   - **A) 2² × 3 × 7** | B) 4 × 21 | C) 2 × 42 | D) 2³ × 7
   - *84 = 4 × 21 = 2² × 3 × 7.*

37. Express 90 as a product of prime factors.
   - **A) 2 × 3² × 5** | B) 2 × 45 | C) 9 × 10 | D) 2² × 3 × 5
   - *90 = 2 × 45 = 2 × 9 × 5 = 2 × 3² × 5.*

38. Express 120 as a product of prime factors.
   - **A) 2³ × 3 × 5** | B) 2² × 30 | C) 4 × 30 | D) 2⁴ × 5
   - *120 = 8 × 15 = 2³ × 3 × 5.*

39. Express 50 as a product of prime factors.
   - A) 2 × 25 | B) 5 × 10 | **C) 2 × 5²** | D) 2² × 5
   - *50 = 2 × 25 = 2 × 5².*

40. Express 150 as a product of prime factors.
   - **A) 2 × 3 × 5²** | B) 3 × 50 | C) 2 × 75 | D) 2² × 3 × 5
   - *150 = 2 × 75 = 2 × 3 × 25 = 2 × 3 × 5².*

41. Express 40 as a product of prime factors.
   - **A) 2³ × 5** | B) 4 × 10 | C) 2² × 10 | D) 8 × 5
   - *40 = 8 × 5 = 2³ × 5.*

42. Which is the correct prime factorisation of 56?
   - **A) 2³ × 7** | B) 2² × 14 | C) 2 × 28 | D) 4 × 14
   - *56 = 8 × 7 = 2³ × 7.*

43. Express 144 as a product of prime factors.
   - **A) 2⁴ × 3²** | B) 2³ × 18 | C) 12² | D) 4 × 36
   - *144 = 16 × 9 = 2⁴ × 3².*

44. Express 200 as a product of prime factors.
   - **A) 2³ × 5²** | B) 2² × 50 | C) 4 × 50 | D) 8 × 25
   - *200 = 8 × 25 = 2³ × 5².*

45. Express 63 as a product of prime factors.
   - **A) 3² × 7** | B) 9 × 7 | C) 3 × 21 | D) 7 × 9
   - *63 = 9 × 7 = 3² × 7. All three forms equal 63, but 3² × 7 uses prime factors in index notation.*

46. Which prime factorisation is written in correct index notation?
   - A) 2 × 2 × 3 | B) 4 × 3 | **C) 2² × 3** | D) 12
   - *Index notation groups repeated prime factors using powers. 2 × 2 × 3 = 2² × 3 is the correct form.*

47. How many prime factors does 12 have (counting multiplicity)?
   - A) 2 | **B) 3** | C) 4 | D) 6
   - *12 = 2 × 2 × 3. That's three prime factors (2, 2, 3) counting with repetition.*

48. Express 98 as a product of prime factors.
   - **A) 2 × 7²** | B) 2 × 49 | C) 7² × 2 | D) 2² × 7
   - *98 = 2 × 49 = 2 × 7². Options A and C are equivalent; A is the standard form.*

49. Express 75 as a product of prime factors.
   - **A) 3 × 5²** | B) 5 × 15 | C) 3 × 25 | D) 5² × 3
   - *75 = 3 × 25 = 3 × 5². Options A and D are the same; A is listed first.*

50. Express 108 as a product of prime factors.
   - **A) 2² × 3³** | B) 4 × 27 | C) 2 × 54 | D) 2³ × 3²
   - *108 = 4 × 27 = 2² × 3³.*

51. Express 252 as a product of prime factors.
   - **A) 2² × 3² × 7** | B) 4 × 63 | C) 2 × 126 | D) 2² × 63
   - *252 = 4 × 63 = 4 × 9 × 7 = 2² × 3² × 7.*

52. How many distinct prime factors does 60 have?
   - A) 2 | **B) 3** | C) 4 | D) 5
   - *60 = 2² × 3 × 5. The distinct prime factors are 2, 3, and 5 — that's 3.*

53. Which number has the prime factorisation 2 × 3 × 5?
   - A) 15 | **B) 30** | C) 60 | D) 45
   - *2 × 3 × 5 = 30.*

54. Which number has the prime factorisation 2² × 7?
   - A) 14 | B) 21 | **C) 28** | D) 56
   - *2² × 7 = 4 × 7 = 28.*

55. Express 180 as a product of prime factors.
   - **A) 2² × 3² × 5** | B) 4 × 45 | C) 2 × 90 | D) 2 × 3 × 30
   - *180 = 4 × 45 = 4 × 9 × 5 = 2² × 3² × 5.*

56. What is the sum of all prime factors (with repetition) of 12?
   - A) 5 | **B) 7** | C) 8 | D) 6
   - *12 = 2 × 2 × 3. Sum = 2 + 2 + 3 = 7.*

57. Which number has the prime factorisation 3² × 5²?
   - A) 45 | B) 75 | **C) 225** | D) 135
   - *3² × 5² = 9 × 25 = 225.*

58. Express 126 as a product of prime factors.
   - **A) 2 × 3² × 7** | B) 2 × 63 | C) 2 × 3 × 21 | D) 2² × 3 × 7
   - *126 = 2 × 63 = 2 × 9 × 7 = 2 × 3² × 7.*

59. Which number has 2⁴ as part of its prime factorisation?
   - A) 24 | B) 36 | **C) 48** | D) 54
   - *48 = 2⁴ × 3. 24 = 2³ × 3, 36 = 2² × 3², 54 = 2 × 3³.*

60. Express 280 as a product of prime factors.
   - **A) 2³ × 5 × 7** | B) 4 × 70 | C) 2² × 5 × 7 | D) 2⁴ × 7
   - *280 = 8 × 35 = 8 × 5 × 7 = 2³ × 5 × 7.*

### SQUARE ROOTS & CUBE ROOTS (Q61–80)

61. Find √144.
   - A) 11 | **B) 12** | C) 13 | D) 14
   - *12² = 144, so √144 = 12. Using prime factors: 144 = 2⁴ × 3² → √144 = 2² × 3 = 12.*

62. Find √225.
   - A) 13 | B) 14 | **C) 15** | D) 16
   - *15² = 225, so √225 = 15. 225 = 3² × 5² → √225 = 3 × 5 = 15.*

63. Find ∛27.
   - **A) 3** | B) 9 | C) 27 | D) 4
   - *3³ = 27, so ∛27 = 3. Or: 27 = 3³ → ∛27 = 3.*

64. Find ∛64.
   - **A) 4** | B) 6 | C) 8 | D) 16
   - *4³ = 64, so ∛64 = 4. Or: 64 = 2⁶ → ∛64 = 2² = 4.*

65. Find √196.
   - A) 12 | B) 13 | **C) 14** | D) 15
   - *14² = 196. Or: 196 = 2² × 7² → √196 = 2 × 7 = 14.*

66. Find ∛125.
   - A) 3 | B) 4 | **C) 5** | D) 6
   - *5³ = 125, so ∛125 = 5. Or: 125 = 5³ → ∛125 = 5.*

67. Find √400.
   - A) 16 | B) 18 | **C) 20** | D) 25
   - *20² = 400. Or: 400 = 2⁴ × 5² → √400 = 2² × 5 = 20.*

68. Find ∛216.
   - A) 4 | B) 5 | **C) 6** | D) 7
   - *6³ = 216. Or: 216 = 2³ × 3³ → ∛216 = 2 × 3 = 6.*

69. Find √324.
   - A) 16 | B) 17 | **C) 18** | D) 19
   - *18² = 324. Or: 324 = 2² × 3⁴ → √324 = 2 × 3² = 18.*

70. Find ∛1000.
   - A) 8 | **B) 10** | C) 12 | D) 15
   - *10³ = 1000, so ∛1000 = 10. Or: 1000 = 2³ × 5³ → ∛1000 = 2 × 5 = 10.*

71. Which of the following is a perfect square?
   - A) 50 | B) 72 | **C) 81** | D) 90
   - *81 = 9² = 3⁴. Its square root is 9, an integer. The others are not perfect squares.*

72. Which of the following is a perfect cube?
   - A) 16 | B) 36 | C) 54 | **D) 125**
   - *125 = 5³. Its cube root is 5. The others are not perfect cubes.*

73. Find √(2⁴ × 3²).
   - A) 6 | **B) 12** | C) 18 | D) 36
   - *√(2⁴ × 3²) = 2² × 3 = 4 × 3 = 12. Halve each index.*

74. Find ∛(2³ × 5³).
   - **A) 10** | B) 25 | C) 30 | D) 50
   - *∛(2³ × 5³) = 2 × 5 = 10. Divide each index by 3.*

75. Find √169.
   - A) 11 | B) 12 | **C) 13** | D) 14
   - *13² = 169, so √169 = 13.*

76. Find ∛512.
   - A) 6 | B) 7 | **C) 8** | D) 9
   - *8³ = 512, so ∛512 = 8. Or: 512 = 2⁹ → ∛512 = 2³ = 8.*

77. Which is NOT a perfect square?
   - A) 36 | B) 49 | C) 64 | **D) 72**
   - *72 = 2³ × 3². For a perfect square, all indices must be even. 72 has an odd index (3 for factor 2).*

78. Find √(5² × 4²).
   - A) 10 | **B) 20** | C) 40 | D) 100
   - *√(5² × 4²) = 5 × 4 = 20. Or: 5² × 4² = 400, and √400 = 20.*

79. Which is NOT a perfect cube?
   - A) 8 | B) 27 | **C) 54** | D) 64
   - *54 = 2 × 3³. For a perfect cube, all indices must be divisible by 3. The index of 2 is 1.*

80. If 3² × 5² × 7² = n², what is n?
   - **A) 3 × 5 × 7** | B) 3 + 5 + 7 | C) (3 × 5 × 7)² | D) 15 × 7
   - *n² = 3² × 5² × 7² = (3 × 5 × 7)², so n = 3 × 5 × 7 = 105.*

### HCF (Q81–110)

81. Find the HCF of 12 and 18.
   - A) 3 | **B) 6** | C) 9 | D) 12
   - *12 = 2² × 3; 18 = 2 × 3². HCF = 2¹ × 3¹ = 6 (take lowest powers of common primes).*

82. Find the HCF of 24 and 36.
   - A) 4 | B) 6 | **C) 12** | D) 24
   - *24 = 2³ × 3; 36 = 2² × 3². HCF = 2² × 3 = 12.*

83. Find the HCF of 15 and 25.
   - A) 3 | **B) 5** | C) 15 | D) 25
   - *15 = 3 × 5; 25 = 5². HCF = 5 (only common prime).*

84. Find the HCF of 8 and 12.
   - A) 2 | B) 3 | **C) 4** | D) 6
   - *8 = 2³; 12 = 2² × 3. HCF = 2² = 4.*

85. Find the HCF of 30 and 45.
   - A) 5 | B) 10 | **C) 15** | D) 30
   - *30 = 2 × 3 × 5; 45 = 3² × 5. HCF = 3 × 5 = 15.*

86. Find the HCF of 16 and 24.
   - A) 4 | B) 6 | **C) 8** | D) 12
   - *16 = 2⁴; 24 = 2³ × 3. HCF = 2³ = 8.*

87. Find the HCF of 20 and 50.
   - A) 5 | **B) 10** | C) 20 | D) 50
   - *20 = 2² × 5; 50 = 2 × 5². HCF = 2 × 5 = 10.*

88. Find the HCF of 36 and 48.
   - A) 6 | B) 8 | **C) 12** | D) 18
   - *36 = 2² × 3²; 48 = 2⁴ × 3. HCF = 2² × 3 = 12.*

89. Find the HCF of 14 and 21.
   - A) 3 | **B) 7** | C) 14 | D) 21
   - *14 = 2 × 7; 21 = 3 × 7. HCF = 7.*

90. Find the HCF of 60 and 90.
   - A) 15 | B) 20 | **C) 30** | D) 45
   - *60 = 2² × 3 × 5; 90 = 2 × 3² × 5. HCF = 2 × 3 × 5 = 30.*

91. Find the HCF of 100 and 150.
   - A) 10 | B) 25 | **C) 50** | D) 75
   - *100 = 2² × 5²; 150 = 2 × 3 × 5². HCF = 2 × 5² = 50.*

92. Find the HCF of 12 and 7.
   - **A) 1** | B) 3 | C) 4 | D) 7
   - *12 = 2² × 3; 7 is prime. They share no common prime factors, so HCF = 1.*

93. Find the HCF of 18 and 27.
   - A) 3 | B) 6 | **C) 9** | D) 18
   - *18 = 2 × 3²; 27 = 3³. HCF = 3² = 9.*

94. Find the HCF of 42 and 56.
   - A) 6 | B) 7 | **C) 14** | D) 21
   - *42 = 2 × 3 × 7; 56 = 2³ × 7. HCF = 2 × 7 = 14.*

95. Find the HCF of 25 and 35.
   - **A) 5** | B) 7 | C) 25 | D) 35
   - *25 = 5²; 35 = 5 × 7. HCF = 5.*

96. Find the HCF of 72 and 108.
   - A) 12 | B) 18 | C) 24 | **D) 36**
   - *72 = 2³ × 3²; 108 = 2² × 3³. HCF = 2² × 3² = 4 × 9 = 36.*

97. What is the HCF of two prime numbers p and q (where p ≠ q)?
   - A) p | B) q | C) pq | **D) 1**
   - *Two different primes share no common factors other than 1, so HCF = 1. They are coprime.*

98. Find the HCF of 48 and 80.
   - A) 8 | B) 12 | **C) 16** | D) 24
   - *48 = 2⁴ × 3; 80 = 2⁴ × 5. HCF = 2⁴ = 16.*

99. Find the HCF of 6, 12, and 18.
   - A) 2 | B) 3 | **C) 6** | D) 12
   - *6 = 2 × 3; 12 = 2² × 3; 18 = 2 × 3². HCF = 2 × 3 = 6 (lowest power of each common prime).*

100. Find the HCF of 4, 8, and 20.
   - A) 1 | B) 2 | **C) 4** | D) 8
   - *4 = 2²; 8 = 2³; 20 = 2² × 5. HCF = 2² = 4.*

101. If HCF(a, b) = 6, which could be a pair (a, b)?
   - A) 6 and 9 | **B) 12 and 18** | C) 6 and 7 | D) 4 and 6
   - *HCF(12, 18) = 6. Check: 12 = 2² × 3; 18 = 2 × 3². HCF = 2 × 3 = 6. ✓*

102. Find the HCF of 90 and 120.
   - A) 10 | B) 15 | **C) 30** | D) 60
   - *90 = 2 × 3² × 5; 120 = 2³ × 3 × 5. HCF = 2 × 3 × 5 = 30.*

103. Find the HCF of 84 and 126.
   - A) 14 | B) 21 | **C) 42** | D) 63
   - *84 = 2² × 3 × 7; 126 = 2 × 3² × 7. HCF = 2 × 3 × 7 = 42.*

104. Two numbers have HCF 4 and LCM 48. One number is 12. Find the other.
   - A) 4 | **B) 16** | C) 24 | D) 48
   - *Use HCF × LCM = product: 4 × 48 = 192. Other number = 192 ÷ 12 = 16.*

105. Find the HCF of 120 and 180.
   - A) 20 | B) 30 | C) 40 | **D) 60**
   - *120 = 2³ × 3 × 5; 180 = 2² × 3² × 5. HCF = 2² × 3 × 5 = 60.*

106. The HCF of 15 and 20 is:
   - A) 3 | B) 4 | **C) 5** | D) 10
   - *15 = 3 × 5; 20 = 2² × 5. HCF = 5.*

107. Find the HCF of 45 and 75.
   - A) 5 | B) 10 | **C) 15** | D) 25
   - *45 = 3² × 5; 75 = 3 × 5². HCF = 3 × 5 = 15.*

108. What is the HCF of 13 and 26?
   - A) 1 | B) 2 | **C) 13** | D) 26
   - *26 = 2 × 13. So 13 divides both 13 and 26. HCF = 13.*

109. Find the HCF of 3, 9, and 15.
   - A) 1 | B) 2 | **C) 3** | D) 9
   - *3 = 3; 9 = 3²; 15 = 3 × 5. Common factor is 3¹. HCF = 3.*

110. Find the HCF of 24 and 60.
   - A) 6 | B) 8 | **C) 12** | D) 24
   - *24 = 2³ × 3; 60 = 2² × 3 × 5. HCF = 2² × 3 = 12.*

### LCM (Q111–140)

111. Find the LCM of 4 and 6.
   - A) 6 | B) 10 | **C) 12** | D) 24
   - *4 = 2²; 6 = 2 × 3. LCM = 2² × 3 = 12 (highest power of each prime).*

112. Find the LCM of 6 and 9.
   - A) 3 | B) 9 | **C) 18** | D) 54
   - *6 = 2 × 3; 9 = 3². LCM = 2 × 3² = 18.*

113. Find the LCM of 12 and 18.
   - A) 6 | B) 18 | **C) 36** | D) 54
   - *12 = 2² × 3; 18 = 2 × 3². LCM = 2² × 3² = 36.*

114. Find the LCM of 5 and 7.
   - A) 12 | B) 15 | **C) 35** | D) 70
   - *5 and 7 are both prime and different. LCM = 5 × 7 = 35.*

115. Find the LCM of 8 and 12.
   - A) 4 | B) 12 | **C) 24** | D) 96
   - *8 = 2³; 12 = 2² × 3. LCM = 2³ × 3 = 24.*

116. Find the LCM of 15 and 20.
   - A) 5 | B) 30 | **C) 60** | D) 300
   - *15 = 3 × 5; 20 = 2² × 5. LCM = 2² × 3 × 5 = 60.*

117. Find the LCM of 3 and 5.
   - A) 3 | B) 5 | C) 8 | **D) 15**
   - *3 and 5 share no common factors. LCM = 3 × 5 = 15.*

118. Find the LCM of 10 and 15.
   - A) 5 | B) 25 | **C) 30** | D) 150
   - *10 = 2 × 5; 15 = 3 × 5. LCM = 2 × 3 × 5 = 30.*

119. Find the LCM of 6 and 8.
   - A) 2 | B) 14 | **C) 24** | D) 48
   - *6 = 2 × 3; 8 = 2³. LCM = 2³ × 3 = 24.*

120. Find the LCM of 4 and 9.
   - A) 1 | B) 13 | **C) 36** | D) 72
   - *4 = 2²; 9 = 3². No common factors. LCM = 2² × 3² = 36.*

121. Find the LCM of 12 and 16.
   - A) 4 | B) 24 | **C) 48** | D) 192
   - *12 = 2² × 3; 16 = 2⁴. LCM = 2⁴ × 3 = 48.*

122. Find the LCM of 20 and 30.
   - A) 10 | B) 30 | **C) 60** | D) 600
   - *20 = 2² × 5; 30 = 2 × 3 × 5. LCM = 2² × 3 × 5 = 60.*

123. Find the LCM of 9 and 15.
   - A) 3 | B) 15 | **C) 45** | D) 135
   - *9 = 3²; 15 = 3 × 5. LCM = 3² × 5 = 45.*

124. Find the LCM of 14 and 21.
   - A) 7 | B) 21 | **C) 42** | D) 294
   - *14 = 2 × 7; 21 = 3 × 7. LCM = 2 × 3 × 7 = 42.*

125. Find the LCM of 2, 3, and 5.
   - A) 10 | B) 15 | **C) 30** | D) 60
   - *2, 3, 5 are all prime and distinct. LCM = 2 × 3 × 5 = 30.*

126. Find the LCM of 4, 6, and 10.
   - A) 30 | **B) 60** | C) 120 | D) 240
   - *4 = 2²; 6 = 2 × 3; 10 = 2 × 5. LCM = 2² × 3 × 5 = 60.*

127. Find the LCM of 25 and 40.
   - A) 5 | B) 100 | **C) 200** | D) 1000
   - *25 = 5²; 40 = 2³ × 5. LCM = 2³ × 5² = 200.*

128. If LCM(a, b) = 36, which could be a pair (a, b)?
   - A) 4 and 8 | **B) 9 and 12** | C) 6 and 8 | D) 4 and 10
   - *LCM(9, 12) = LCM(3², 2² × 3) = 2² × 3² = 36. ✓*

129. Find the LCM of 18 and 24.
   - A) 6 | B) 36 | **C) 72** | D) 432
   - *18 = 2 × 3²; 24 = 2³ × 3. LCM = 2³ × 3² = 72.*

130. Find the LCM of 6, 8, and 9.
   - A) 18 | B) 24 | C) 36 | **D) 72**
   - *6 = 2 × 3; 8 = 2³; 9 = 3². LCM = 2³ × 3² = 72.*

131. Two buses depart at the same time. Bus A comes every 12 min, Bus B every 18 min. When do they next depart together?
   - A) 6 min | B) 24 min | **C) 36 min** | D) 72 min
   - *Next joint departure = LCM(12, 18) = 36 minutes.*

132. Find the LCM of 30 and 45.
   - A) 15 | B) 45 | **C) 90** | D) 135
   - *30 = 2 × 3 × 5; 45 = 3² × 5. LCM = 2 × 3² × 5 = 90.*

133. Find the LCM of 16 and 20.
   - A) 4 | B) 40 | **C) 80** | D) 320
   - *16 = 2⁴; 20 = 2² × 5. LCM = 2⁴ × 5 = 80.*

134. HCF(12, 18) = 6 and LCM(12, 18) = 36. Verify: HCF × LCM = ?
   - A) 54 | B) 72 | C) 108 | **D) 216**
   - *6 × 36 = 216. Also 12 × 18 = 216. The relationship HCF × LCM = product of the two numbers holds.*

135. Find the LCM of 5, 6, and 10.
   - A) 10 | B) 20 | **C) 30** | D) 60
   - *5 = 5; 6 = 2 × 3; 10 = 2 × 5. LCM = 2 × 3 × 5 = 30.*

136. Find the LCM of 3, 4, and 6.
   - **A) 12** | B) 18 | C) 24 | D) 36
   - *3 = 3; 4 = 2²; 6 = 2 × 3. LCM = 2² × 3 = 12.*

137. Which is larger, LCM(4, 6) or LCM(3, 8)?
   - A) LCM(4,6) = 12 | **B) LCM(3,8) = 24** | C) They are equal | D) Cannot tell
   - *LCM(4,6) = 12; LCM(3,8) = 24. LCM(3, 8) is larger.*

138. Find the LCM of 2, 4, and 8.
   - A) 2 | B) 4 | **C) 8** | D) 16
   - *2 = 2; 4 = 2²; 8 = 2³. LCM = 2³ = 8.*

139. Lights flash together at 0 seconds. Light A flashes every 6 s, Light B every 10 s. When do they next flash together?
   - A) 16 s | B) 20 s | **C) 30 s** | D) 60 s
   - *LCM(6, 10) = 30 seconds.*

140. Find the LCM of 8 and 20.
   - A) 4 | B) 20 | **C) 40** | D) 160
   - *8 = 2³; 20 = 2² × 5. LCM = 2³ × 5 = 40.*

### MIXED / APPLIED (Q141–150)

141. The HCF of 24 and 36 is 12. Their LCM is:
   - A) 48 | **B) 72** | C) 108 | D) 144
   - *HCF × LCM = 24 × 36 = 864. LCM = 864 ÷ 12 = 72.*

142. Find the smallest number divisible by both 12 and 15.
   - A) 3 | B) 30 | **C) 60** | D) 180
   - *Smallest number divisible by both = LCM(12, 15). 12 = 2² × 3; 15 = 3 × 5. LCM = 2² × 3 × 5 = 60.*

143. What is the largest number that divides both 48 and 60?
   - A) 6 | B) 8 | **C) 12** | D) 24
   - *Largest number that divides both = HCF(48, 60). 48 = 2⁴ × 3; 60 = 2² × 3 × 5. HCF = 2² × 3 = 12.*

144. A rope 72 cm long is cut into equal pieces with no waste. Which is the greatest length from the options that gives more than one piece?
   - A) 6 | B) 8 | C) 9 | **D) 12**
   - *72 = 2³ × 3². All four options divide 72 evenly. The greatest is 12, giving 72 ÷ 12 = 6 equal pieces.*

145. Which of the following is a common multiple of 4 and 6?
   - A) 10 | B) 14 | **C) 24** | D) 26
   - *24 = 4 × 6. Multiples of 4: 4, 8, 12, 16, 20, 24… Multiples of 6: 6, 12, 18, 24… 24 appears in both.*

146. Express 360 as a product of prime factors.
   - **A) 2³ × 3² × 5** | B) 2² × 3² × 10 | C) 2⁴ × 3 × 5 | D) 2³ × 3 × 5²
   - *360 = 8 × 45 = 8 × 9 × 5 = 2³ × 3² × 5.*

147. Find the HCF and LCM of 12 and 20. What is HCF + LCM?
   - A) 62 | **B) 64** | C) 66 | D) 68
   - *12 = 2² × 3; 20 = 2² × 5. HCF = 2² = 4; LCM = 2² × 3 × 5 = 60. HCF + LCM = 4 + 60 = 64.*

148. Two numbers are 2² × 3 and 2 × 3². Their HCF is:
   - **A) 6** | B) 12 | C) 18 | D) 36
   - *2² × 3 = 12; 2 × 3² = 18. HCF = 2¹ × 3¹ = 6 (lowest power of each common prime).*

149. Two numbers are 2² × 3 and 2 × 3². Their LCM is:
   - A) 12 | B) 18 | **C) 36** | D) 72
   - *2² × 3 = 12; 2 × 3² = 18. LCM = 2² × 3² = 4 × 9 = 36 (highest power of each prime).*

150. √(4 × 9 × 25) equals:
   - A) 15 | B) 25 | **C) 30** | D) 38
   - *√(4 × 9 × 25) = √4 × √9 × √25 = 2 × 3 × 5 = 30.*

---

## Topic 2: Integers, Rational & Real Numbers
*Negative numbers, operations with integers, real number system* — 151 questions

### NUMBER SYSTEM CLASSIFICATION (Q1–20)

1. Which of the following is an integer?
   - A) 0.5 | B) √2 | **C) −7** | D) ⅔
   - *Integers are whole numbers including negatives: …, −2, −1, 0, 1, 2, … −7 is an integer.*

2. Which of the following is NOT a rational number?
   - A) 0.5 | B) −3 | **C) √5** | D) ¾
   - *√5 is irrational — its decimal expansion is non-terminating and non-recurring. The others can be written as fractions.*

3. Which of the following is a natural number?
   - A) 0 | B) −1 | C) ½ | **D) 7**
   - *Natural numbers are the counting numbers: 1, 2, 3, … 7 is a natural number. 0 and negatives are excluded.*

4. π (pi) belongs to which set?
   - A) Integers | B) Rational numbers | **C) Irrational numbers** | D) Natural numbers
   - *π = 3.14159… is non-terminating and non-recurring, so it is irrational.*

5. Which statement is true?
   - A) All integers are natural numbers | **B) All natural numbers are integers** | C) All rational numbers are integers | D) All real numbers are rational
   - *Natural numbers (1, 2, 3, …) are a subset of integers (…, −1, 0, 1, 2, …). So all natural numbers are integers.*

6. 0.333… (recurring) is:
   - A) Irrational | B) An integer | **C) Rational** | D) Natural
   - *0.333… = 1/3. Recurring decimals are rational — they can be written as fractions.*

7. Which of these is irrational?
   - A) 0.25 | B) √9 | **C) √7** | D) −4
   - *√7 ≈ 2.6457… is non-terminating and non-recurring. √9 = 3 (rational), 0.25 = ¼ (rational), −4 (integer).*

8. Which set contains ALL of the following: −5, 0, 3, ½?
   - A) Integers | B) Natural numbers | **C) Rational numbers** | D) Irrational numbers
   - *Rational numbers include integers, fractions, and zero. ½ is not an integer, so integers don't work. Rational fits all four.*

9. Which of the following is a rational number?
   - A) √2 | B) √3 | **C) √4** | D) √5
   - *√4 = 2, which is an integer and therefore rational. The others are irrational.*

10. Is −3.75 a rational number?
   - A) No, it is negative | B) No, it is a decimal | **C) Yes, it equals −15/4** | D) Yes, but only because it is negative
   - *−3.75 = −15/4, a ratio of two integers. All terminating decimals are rational.*

11. Which number is between −3 and −1 on the number line?
   - A) −4 | B) 0 | **C) −2** | D) 1
   - *−3 < −2 < −1, so −2 lies between −3 and −1.*

12. Which set does NOT include 0?
   - A) Integers | B) Rational numbers | **C) Natural numbers** | D) Real numbers
   - *Natural numbers start at 1: {1, 2, 3, …}. Zero is not a natural number.*

13. Which is the correct ordering from smallest to largest?
   - **A) −5, −3, 0, 2** | B) −3, −5, 0, 2 | C) 0, −3, 2, −5 | D) 2, 0, −3, −5
   - *On the number line: −5 < −3 < 0 < 2.*

14. The absolute value |−8| equals:
   - A) −8 | B) 0 | **C) 8** | D) 16
   - *The absolute value of a number is its distance from zero, always non-negative. |−8| = 8.*

15. Which of the following is true?
   - A) |−5| < |3| | **B) |−5| > |3|** | C) |−5| = |3| | D) |−5| = −5
   - *|−5| = 5 and |3| = 3. Since 5 > 3, |−5| > |3|.*

16. Which is larger: −0.1 or −10?
   - A) −10 | **B) −0.1** | C) They are equal | D) Cannot compare
   - *On the number line, −0.1 is closer to 0 and therefore greater. −0.1 > −10.*

17. Which of the following correctly classifies √16?
   - A) Irrational only | B) Rational only | C) Both integer and rational | **D) Natural, integer, and rational**
   - *√16 = 4. Since 4 is a natural number, it is also an integer and a rational number.*

18. A recurring decimal is always:
   - A) Irrational | B) An integer | **C) Rational** | D) Natural
   - *Recurring decimals can be written as fractions, so they are rational. e.g. 0.7̄ = 7/9.*

19. Which number line correctly shows −2 to the left of −1?
   - **A) Always true** | B) Only true for positive numbers | C) Never true | D) Sometimes true
   - *On the number line, more negative means further left. −2 is always to the left of −1.*

20. How many integers are there between −4 and 4 (exclusive)?
   - A) 6 | **B) 7** | C) 8 | D) 9
   - *Integers between −4 and 4 (not including −4 and 4): −3, −2, −1, 0, 1, 2, 3 — that's 7.*

### ADDITION & SUBTRACTION OF INTEGERS (Q21–55)

21. Calculate −3 + (−4).
   - A) 7 | **B) −7** | C) 1 | D) −1
   - *−3 + (−4): same signs (both negative), add and keep negative. 3 + 4 = 7, so answer is −7.*

22. Calculate 7 + (−3).
   - A) −4 | **B) 4** | C) 10 | D) −10
   - *7 + (−3): different signs, subtract. 7 − 3 = 4. Larger number (7) is positive, so answer is +4.*

23. Calculate −8 + 3.
   - A) 11 | B) −11 | C) 5 | **D) −5**
   - *−8 + 3: different signs. 8 − 3 = 5. Larger (8) is negative, so answer is −5.*

24. Calculate 5 − 9.
   - A) 14 | B) −14 | C) 4 | **D) −4**
   - *5 − 9 = −4. Since we're taking more than we have, result is negative.*

25. Calculate −6 − 2.
   - **A) −8** | B) 8 | C) −4 | D) 4
   - *−6 − 2 = −6 + (−2). Same signs, add: 6 + 2 = 8, keep negative → −8.*

26. Calculate 4 − (−3).
   - A) 1 | B) −1 | **C) 7** | D) −7
   - *Subtracting a negative is adding: 4 − (−3) = 4 + 3 = 7.*

27. Calculate −5 − (−2).
   - A) −7 | B) 7 | **C) −3** | D) 3
   - *−5 − (−2) = −5 + 2 = −3. Subtracting a negative becomes addition.*

28. Calculate −10 + 10.
   - A) 20 | B) −20 | **C) 0** | D) 100
   - *A number plus its opposite always equals zero. −10 + 10 = 0.*

29. Calculate 3 − (−7).
   - A) −4 | B) 4 | **C) 10** | D) −10
   - *3 − (−7) = 3 + 7 = 10.*

30. Calculate −9 + 4.
   - A) 13 | B) −13 | C) 5 | **D) −5**
   - *−9 + 4: different signs. 9 − 4 = 5. Larger (9) is negative → −5.*

31. Calculate −2 + (−8).
   - A) 6 | B) −6 | C) 10 | **D) −10**
   - *−2 + (−8) = −(2 + 8) = −10. Same signs, add and keep negative.*

32. Calculate 0 − 6.
   - A) 6 | **B) −6** | C) 0 | D) 60
   - *0 − 6 = −6.*

33. Calculate −15 + 8.
   - A) 23 | B) −23 | C) 7 | **D) −7**
   - *−15 + 8: different signs. 15 − 8 = 7. Larger (15) is negative → −7.*

34. Calculate 12 − 20.
   - A) 8 | **B) −8** | C) 32 | D) −32
   - *12 − 20 = −8. We're 8 short of zero after going 12 up and 20 down.*

35. Calculate −4 − (−9).
   - A) −13 | B) 13 | **C) 5** | D) −5
   - *−4 − (−9) = −4 + 9 = 5. Subtract negative → add.*

36. Calculate (−3) + (−3) + (−3).
   - A) 9 | **B) −9** | C) 0 | D) −27
   - *Three lots of −3: −3 + −3 + −3 = −9. Or: 3 × (−3) = −9.*

37. Calculate −1 − 1.
   - A) 0 | B) 2 | **C) −2** | D) 1
   - *−1 − 1 = −1 + (−1) = −2.*

38. Calculate 100 − 150.
   - A) 250 | B) −250 | C) 50 | **D) −50**
   - *100 − 150 = −50.*

39. Calculate −20 − (−8).
   - A) −28 | B) 28 | **C) −12** | D) 12
   - *−20 − (−8) = −20 + 8 = −12.*

40. The temperature drops from 3°C to −5°C. By how many degrees did it drop?
   - A) 2 | B) −2 | **C) 8** | D) −8
   - *Change = −5 − 3 = −8. The temperature dropped by 8 degrees.*

41. Calculate −6 + 6 − 3.
   - **A) −3** | B) 3 | C) 9 | D) −9
   - *−6 + 6 = 0; 0 − 3 = −3.*

42. Calculate 5 − 8 + 3.
   - **A) 0** | B) −6 | C) 6 | D) 16
   - *5 − 8 = −3; −3 + 3 = 0.*

43. Calculate −4 + 10 − 9.
   - **A) −3** | B) 3 | C) 23 | D) −23
   - *−4 + 10 = 6; 6 − 9 = −3.*

44. Calculate −7 − 3 + 5.
   - **A) −5** | B) 5 | C) −15 | D) 15
   - *−7 − 3 = −10; −10 + 5 = −5.*

45. Calculate 2 − 5 − 4.
   - **A) −7** | B) 7 | C) 11 | D) −11
   - *2 − 5 = −3; −3 − 4 = −7.*

46. What must be added to −8 to get 2?
   - A) −6 | B) 6 | **C) 10** | D) −10
   - *−8 + ? = 2. ? = 2 − (−8) = 2 + 8 = 10.*

47. Calculate −3 + 5 − 2 + 1.
   - **A) 1** | B) −1 | C) 11 | D) −11
   - *−3 + 5 = 2; 2 − 2 = 0; 0 + 1 = 1.*

48. Calculate −(−5).
   - A) −5 | B) 0 | **C) 5** | D) 25
   - *The negative of a negative is positive. −(−5) = +5 = 5.*

49. On a number line, what is 3 steps left from −2?
   - A) 1 | B) 5 | **C) −5** | D) −1
   - *−2 − 3 = −5. Moving left (subtracting) from −2 by 3 gives −5.*

50. Calculate −11 + 4 + 7.
   - **A) 0** | B) −14 | C) 14 | D) 2
   - *−11 + 4 = −7; −7 + 7 = 0.*

51. Calculate 8 − (−1) − 3.
   - A) 4 | **B) 6** | C) 10 | D) −6
   - *8 − (−1) = 8 + 1 = 9; 9 − 3 = 6.*

52. What is the difference between −3 and 5?
   - A) 2 | **B) 8** | C) −8 | D) −2
   - *Difference = 5 − (−3) = 5 + 3 = 8. Or |5 − (−3)| = 8.*

53. Calculate −50 + 30 + 10.
   - **A) −10** | B) 10 | C) 90 | D) −90
   - *−50 + 30 = −20; −20 + 10 = −10.*

54. A diver is at −30 m. She rises 12 m. What is her new depth?
   - **A) −18 m** | B) 18 m | C) −42 m | D) 42 m
   - *−30 + 12 = −18 m. She is still below sea level.*

55. Calculate −999 + 1000.
   - A) −1 | B) 0 | **C) 1** | D) 1999
   - *−999 + 1000 = 1.*

### MULTIPLICATION & DIVISION OF INTEGERS (Q56–90)

56. Calculate (−3) × 4.
   - A) 12 | **B) −12** | C) 7 | D) −7
   - *Positive × Negative = Negative. 3 × 4 = 12, so (−3) × 4 = −12.*

57. Calculate (−5) × (−6).
   - A) −30 | **B) 30** | C) −11 | D) 11
   - *Negative × Negative = Positive. 5 × 6 = 30, so (−5) × (−6) = +30.*

58. Calculate 8 × (−3).
   - A) 24 | **B) −24** | C) 5 | D) −5
   - *Positive × Negative = Negative. 8 × 3 = 24, so answer is −24.*

59. Calculate (−7) × (−7).
   - A) −49 | **B) 49** | C) 14 | D) −14
   - *Negative × Negative = Positive. 7 × 7 = 49.*

60. Calculate (−2) × (−3) × (−1).
   - A) 6 | **B) −6** | C) −5 | D) 5
   - *(−2) × (−3) = +6; then 6 × (−1) = −6. Three negative signs → negative result.*

61. Calculate (−4) × 0.
   - A) −4 | B) 4 | **C) 0** | D) undefined
   - *Any number multiplied by 0 is 0.*

62. Calculate (−12) ÷ 4.
   - A) 3 | **B) −3** | C) 8 | D) −8
   - *Negative ÷ Positive = Negative. 12 ÷ 4 = 3, so answer is −3.*

63. Calculate 20 ÷ (−5).
   - A) 4 | **B) −4** | C) −15 | D) 15
   - *Positive ÷ Negative = Negative. 20 ÷ 5 = 4, so answer is −4.*

64. Calculate (−18) ÷ (−3).
   - A) −6 | **B) 6** | C) −15 | D) 15
   - *Negative ÷ Negative = Positive. 18 ÷ 3 = 6.*

65. Calculate (−6)².
   - A) −36 | **B) 36** | C) −12 | D) 12
   - *(−6)² = (−6) × (−6) = +36. Squaring any real number gives a non-negative result.*

66. Calculate −6².
   - A) 36 | **B) −36** | C) 12 | D) −12
   - *−6² means −(6²) = −36. The square applies only to 6, then the negative is applied.*

67. Which product is positive?
   - A) (−2)(3) | **B) (−2)(−3)** | C) (2)(−3) | D) All are negative
   - *(−2)(−3) = +6. Two negatives make a positive.*

68. Calculate (−1)¹⁰⁰.
   - A) −1 | **B) 1** | C) 100 | D) −100
   - *(−1) raised to an even power is always +1. 100 is even, so (−1)¹⁰⁰ = 1.*

69. Calculate (−1)⁹⁹.
   - **A) −1** | B) 1 | C) 99 | D) −99
   - *(−1) raised to an odd power is −1. 99 is odd, so (−1)⁹⁹ = −1.*

70. Calculate (−3)³.
   - A) 9 | B) −9 | C) 27 | **D) −27**
   - *(−3)³ = (−3)(−3)(−3) = 9 × (−3) = −27. Odd power keeps the negative.*

71. Calculate 36 ÷ (−9).
   - A) 4 | **B) −4** | C) 27 | D) −27
   - *Positive ÷ Negative = Negative. 36 ÷ 9 = 4, so answer is −4.*

72. Calculate (−2) × 3 × (−5).
   - **A) 30** | B) −30 | C) −10 | D) 10
   - *(−2) × 3 = −6; (−6) × (−5) = +30. Two negatives → positive.*

73. Calculate (−4) × (−2) × (−3).
   - A) 24 | **B) −24** | C) −9 | D) 9
   - *(−4)(−2) = 8; 8 × (−3) = −24. Three negatives → negative.*

74. What is (−45) ÷ (−9)?
   - A) −5 | **B) 5** | C) −4 | D) 4
   - *Negative ÷ Negative = Positive. 45 ÷ 9 = 5.*

75. Which of the following equals −8?
   - A) (−4) × (−2) | B) (4) × (2) | **C) (−4) × 2** | D) (4) × (−2)
   - *(−4) × 2 = −8. Negative × Positive = Negative.*

76. Calculate (−2)⁴.
   - A) −16 | **B) 16** | C) −8 | D) 8
   - *(−2)⁴ = (−2)(−2)(−2)(−2) = 4 × 4 = 16. Even power → positive.*

77. Calculate (−10) ÷ 2 × (−1).
   - **A) 5** | B) −5 | C) 20 | D) −20
   - *Working left to right: (−10) ÷ 2 = −5; (−5) × (−1) = +5.*

78. If (−a) × b = 12, and b = −3, find a.
   - A) −4 | **B) 4** | C) −36 | D) 36
   - *(−a)(−3) = 12 → 3a = 12 → a = 4.*

79. Calculate (−3) × (−4) ÷ (−2).
   - A) 6 | **B) −6** | C) 24 | D) −24
   - *(−3)(−4) = 12; 12 ÷ (−2) = −6.*

80. What is the sign of a product of 5 negative numbers?
   - A) Positive | **B) Negative** | C) Zero | D) Cannot tell
   - *5 is odd. The product of an odd number of negative numbers is negative.*

81. Calculate (−100) ÷ (−10) ÷ (−2).
   - A) 5 | **B) −5** | C) 20 | D) −20
   - *(−100) ÷ (−10) = 10; 10 ÷ (−2) = −5.*

82. What is (−6) × (−6) × 0?
   - A) 36 | B) −36 | **C) 0** | D) Cannot determine
   - *Anything multiplied by 0 is 0, regardless of other factors.*

83. Calculate (−3) × 4 − 2.
   - A) −10 | **B) −14** | C) 10 | D) 14
   - *(−3) × 4 = −12 first (multiplication before subtraction). −12 − 2 = −14.*

84. Which is the correct value of (−2)³?
   - A) 6 | B) −6 | C) 8 | **D) −8**
   - *(−2)³ = (−2)(−2)(−2) = 4 × (−2) = −8.*

85. Calculate (−1) × (−2) × (−3) × (−4).
   - **A) 24** | B) −24 | C) 10 | D) −10
   - *4 negatives → positive. 1 × 2 × 3 × 4 = 24, so answer is +24.*

86. A submarine descends 5 m each second for 8 seconds. What is its depth change?
   - A) 40 m | **B) −40 m** | C) 3 m | D) −3 m
   - *8 × (−5) = −40 m. The submarine is 40 m deeper (represented as −40 m).*

87. Calculate (−56) ÷ 7.
   - A) 8 | **B) −8** | C) 63 | D) −63
   - *Negative ÷ Positive = Negative. 56 ÷ 7 = 8, so (−56) ÷ 7 = −8.*

88. What sign does (−a)² always have when a ≠ 0?
   - A) Always negative | **B) Always positive** | C) Depends on a | D) Could be zero
   - *(−a)² = (−a)(−a) = a². Squaring always gives a positive result (for non-zero a).*

89. Calculate (−2)² − (−2)³.
   - A) 4 | **B) 12** | C) −4 | D) −12
   - *(−2)² = 4; (−2)³ = −8. 4 − (−8) = 4 + 8 = 12.*

90. If you multiply a negative number by a positive number, the result is:
   - A) Always positive | **B) Always negative** | C) Always zero | D) Could be positive or negative
   - *Negative × Positive = Negative. Always.*

### ORDER OF OPERATIONS / BODMAS (Q91–120)

91. Calculate 3 + 4 × 2.
   - A) 14 | **B) 11** | C) 10 | D) 24
   - *Multiplication before addition: 4 × 2 = 8, then 3 + 8 = 11.*

92. Calculate (3 + 4) × 2.
   - A) 11 | **B) 14** | C) 10 | D) 24
   - *Brackets first: (3 + 4) = 7, then 7 × 2 = 14.*

93. Calculate 20 − 4 × 3.
   - A) 48 | **B) 8** | C) 24 | D) 16
   - *Multiplication first: 4 × 3 = 12, then 20 − 12 = 8.*

94. Calculate 2 + 3² × 2.
   - A) 50 | **B) 20** | C) 16 | D) 11
   - *Order (power) first: 3² = 9; then multiply: 9 × 2 = 18; then add: 2 + 18 = 20.*

95. Calculate 10 ÷ 2 + 3.
   - **A) 8** | B) 2 | C) 10 | D) 11
   - *Division before addition: 10 ÷ 2 = 5, then 5 + 3 = 8.*

96. Calculate 10 ÷ (2 + 3).
   - A) 8 | **B) 2** | C) 10 | D) 11
   - *Brackets first: 2 + 3 = 5, then 10 ÷ 5 = 2.*

97. Calculate −3² + 1.
   - A) 10 | **B) −8** | C) −9 | D) 7
   - *Powers before addition: 3² = 9, so −3² = −9. Then −9 + 1 = −8.*

98. Calculate (−3)² + 1.
   - **A) 10** | B) −8 | C) −9 | D) 7
   - *(−3)² = 9 first. Then 9 + 1 = 10.*

99. Calculate 4 + 8 ÷ 2 − 1.
   - A) 5 | **B) 7** | C) 4 | D) 9
   - *Division first: 8 ÷ 2 = 4. Then left to right: 4 + 4 − 1 = 7.*

100. Calculate 3 × 4 + 2 × 5.
   - A) 70 | **B) 22** | C) 17 | D) 50
   - *Multiplications first: 3 × 4 = 12 and 2 × 5 = 10. Then 12 + 10 = 22.*

101. Calculate 5 × (2 + 3) − 4².
   - **A) 9** | B) −9 | C) 11 | D) −11
   - *Brackets: 2 + 3 = 5. Power: 4² = 16. Then: 5 × 5 − 16 = 25 − 16 = 9.*

102. Calculate (−2)³ + 3².
   - **A) 1** | B) 17 | C) −17 | D) −1
   - *(−2)³ = −8; 3² = 9. Then −8 + 9 = 1.*

103. Calculate 6 ÷ 2 × 3.
   - A) 1 | **B) 9** | C) 12 | D) 4
   - *Division and multiplication have equal priority — work left to right. 6 ÷ 2 = 3, then 3 × 3 = 9.*

104. Calculate 15 − 3 × (4 − 2).
   - A) 24 | **B) 9** | C) 27 | D) 3
   - *Brackets: 4 − 2 = 2. Multiply: 3 × 2 = 6. Subtract: 15 − 6 = 9.*

105. Calculate 2³ − 4 ÷ 2.
   - A) 2 | **B) 6** | C) 0 | D) 10
   - *Powers: 2³ = 8. Division: 4 ÷ 2 = 2. Then 8 − 2 = 6.*

106. Calculate −(4 − 7).
   - A) −3 | **B) 3** | C) 11 | D) −11
   - *Brackets: 4 − 7 = −3. Then −(−3) = +3.*

107. Calculate 1 + 2 × 3 − 4 ÷ 2.
   - A) 1.5 | **B) 5** | C) 3 | D) 10
   - *Multiply and divide first: 2 × 3 = 6; 4 ÷ 2 = 2. Then: 1 + 6 − 2 = 5.*

108. Calculate 3 × [4 + 2 × (5 − 3)].
   - **A) 24** | B) 36 | C) 30 | D) 18
   - *Inner brackets: 5 − 3 = 2. Multiply inside: 2 × 2 = 4. Bracket: 4 + 4 = 8. Outer: 3 × 8 = 24.*

109. Calculate 4² ÷ (8 − 4).
   - **A) 4** | B) 8 | C) 16 | D) 2
   - *Power: 4² = 16. Brackets: 8 − 4 = 4. Then 16 ÷ 4 = 4.*

110. Calculate (−4 + 1) × (3 − 5).
   - **A) 6** | B) −6 | C) 14 | D) −14
   - *(−4 + 1) = −3; (3 − 5) = −2. Then (−3) × (−2) = +6.*

111. Calculate 5 + 3 × 2².
   - **A) 17** | B) 64 | C) 27 | D) 23
   - *Power: 2² = 4. Multiply: 3 × 4 = 12. Add: 5 + 12 = 17.*

112. Calculate 12 ÷ 4 × 3 − 2².
   - **A) 5** | B) 17 | C) 1 | D) −1
   - *Division: 12 ÷ 4 = 3. Multiply: 3 × 3 = 9. Power: 2² = 4. Then 9 − 4 = 5.*

113. Calculate (−2 + 5)² − 4.
   - **A) 5** | B) 23 | C) −5 | D) 1
   - *Bracket: −2 + 5 = 3. Power: 3² = 9. Then 9 − 4 = 5.*

114. Which expression equals 14?
   - **A) 2 + 3 × 4** | B) (2 + 3) × 4 | C) 2 × 3 + 4 | D) 2 + 3 + 4
   - *2 + 3 × 4 = 2 + 12 = 14 (multiply first). (2+3)×4 = 20, 2×3+4 = 10, 2+3+4 = 9.*

115. Calculate 3 + (−2)² × 2.
   - **A) 11** | B) 6 | C) 10 | D) −5
   - *(−2)² = 4; 4 × 2 = 8; 3 + 8 = 11.*

116. Calculate 50 ÷ (5 × 2).
   - A) 20 | **B) 5** | C) 25 | D) 10
   - *Brackets first: 5 × 2 = 10. Then 50 ÷ 10 = 5.*

117. Calculate −2 × 3 + 4 × (−1).
   - A) 2 | B) −2 | **C) −10** | D) 10
   - *−2 × 3 = −6; 4 × (−1) = −4; then −6 + (−4) = −10.*

118. Calculate 7 − 2 × (3 + 1).
   - **A) −1** | B) 20 | C) 15 | D) 11
   - *Brackets: 3 + 1 = 4. Multiply: 2 × 4 = 8. Subtract: 7 − 8 = −1.*

119. Calculate (10 − 4) ÷ (3 − 1) × 3.
   - A) 3 | **B) 9** | C) 18 | D) 15
   - *Brackets: (10−4) = 6; (3−1) = 2. Then 6 ÷ 2 = 3; 3 × 3 = 9.*

120. Calculate 2 × 3² − (5 − 3)³.
   - **A) 10** | B) 6 | C) 26 | D) 14
   - *3² = 9; (5−3)³ = 2³ = 8. Then 2 × 9 − 8 = 18 − 8 = 10.*

### MIXED / RATIONAL NUMBER PROBLEMS (Q121–150)

121. Calculate (−3 + 7) × (2² − 6).
   - A) 8 | **B) −8** | C) 0 | D) −24
   - *(−3+7) = 4; (2²−6) = (4−6) = −2. Then 4 × (−2) = −8.*

122. Which of these is a terminating decimal?
   - A) 1/3 | B) 1/6 | **C) 1/4** | D) 1/7
   - *1/4 = 0.25, which terminates. 1/3 = 0.333…, 1/6 = 0.1666…, 1/7 = 0.142857… all recur.*

123. Express 0.6̄ (0.666…) as a fraction.
   - A) 6/10 | **B) 2/3** | C) 3/5 | D) 6/9
   - *Let x = 0.666… Then 10x = 6.666… Subtract: 9x = 6, so x = 6/9 = 2/3.*

124. Which fraction equals a terminating decimal?
   - A) 1/3 | B) 2/7 | **C) 3/8** | D) 5/6
   - *3/8 = 0.375. A fraction terminates if its denominator (in lowest terms) has only factors of 2 and 5.*

125. Calculate −½ + ¾.
   - **A) ¼** | B) −¼ | C) 1 | D) −1
   - *−½ = −2/4; −2/4 + 3/4 = 1/4 = ¼.*

126. Is √2 rational or irrational?
   - A) Rational, since 2 is rational | B) Rational, since it terminates | **C) Irrational, since its decimal is non-terminating non-recurring** | D) Irrational, since 2 is prime
   - *√2 = 1.41421356… is non-terminating and non-recurring, so it is irrational.*

127. Calculate −¾ × (−8).
   - A) −6 | **B) 6** | C) −⁶⁄₃₂ | D) 2
   - *−¾ × (−8) = +(¾ × 8) = 8×3/4 = 24/4 = 6. Negative × Negative = Positive.*

128. The product of two negative integers is always:
   - A) Negative | **B) Positive** | C) Zero | D) Undefined
   - *Negative × Negative = Positive. Always.*

129. Which correctly orders these from least to greatest: −½, −2, 0.5, −0.1?
   - **A) −2, −½, −0.1, 0.5** | B) −0.1, −½, −2, 0.5 | C) 0.5, −0.1, −½, −2 | D) −½, −2, −0.1, 0.5
   - *Convert to decimals: −2, −0.5, 0.5, −0.1. Ordering: −2 < −0.5 < −0.1 < 0.5.*

130. Which number is closest to 0 on the number line?
   - A) −10 | **B) −0.01** | C) 0.5 | D) −3
   - *Distance from 0: |−10| = 10, |−0.01| = 0.01, |0.5| = 0.5, |−3| = 3. Smallest distance is 0.01.*

131. Calculate (−¼) ÷ ½.
   - **A) −½** | B) ½ | C) −⅛ | D) ⅛
   - *Dividing by ½ is multiplying by 2: (−¼) × 2 = −½.*

132. Which of the following has the greatest value?
   - A) −100 | **B) −0.001** | C) −1000 | D) −10
   - *On the number line, −0.001 is closest to zero and therefore the greatest among these negatives.*

133. Calculate 5 − (−3) × 2.
   - A) 4 | **B) 11** | C) 16 | D) −1
   - *Multiplication first: (−3) × 2 = −6. Then 5 − (−6) = 5 + 6 = 11.*

134. If the temperature at midnight is −8°C and rises by 12°C by noon, what is the noon temperature?
   - A) −20°C | **B) 4°C** | C) 20°C | D) −4°C
   - *−8 + 12 = 4°C.*

135. A company loses $500 per month for 6 months. What is the total change in profit?
   - A) $3000 | **B) −$3000** | C) $500 | D) −$500
   - *6 × (−500) = −3000. The total change is −$3000 (a loss of $3000).*

136. Which of these is NOT an integer?
   - A) −4 | B) 0 | C) √9 | **D) 0.5**
   - *0.5 = ½ is not a whole number, so not an integer. −4, 0, and √9 = 3 are all integers.*

137. Calculate (−3 + 1)³.
   - A) 8 | **B) −8** | C) 6 | D) −6
   - *Brackets: −3 + 1 = −2. Then (−2)³ = −8.*

138. What is (−4) ÷ (½)?
   - A) −2 | B) 2 | **C) −8** | D) 8
   - *Dividing by ½ is multiplying by 2: (−4) × 2 = −8.*

139. Which value of n satisfies −n = 5?
   - A) 5 | **B) −5** | C) 0 | D) −10
   - *If −n = 5, then n = −5. Check: −(−5) = 5 ✓*

140. Calculate (−2)² + (−2)² + (−2)².
   - A) −24 | B) −12 | **C) 12** | D) 24
   - *(−2)² = 4. So 4 + 4 + 4 = 12.*

141. Between which two consecutive integers does √20 lie?
   - **A) 4 and 5** | B) 3 and 4 | C) 5 and 6 | D) 2 and 3
   - *4² = 16 and 5² = 25. Since 16 < 20 < 25, we have 4 < √20 < 5.*

142. Calculate −3 × (−2)² ÷ (−1)³.
   - **A) 12** | B) −12 | C) 6 | D) −6
   - *(−2)² = 4; (−1)³ = −1. Then −3 × 4 = −12; −12 ÷ (−1) = 12.*

143. Is the sum of two irrational numbers always irrational?
   - A) Yes, always | **B) No, it can be rational** | C) No, it is always rational | D) It is always zero
   - *Example: √2 + (−√2) = 0, which is rational. The sum of two irrationals can be rational.*

144. Calculate |−3 + (−4)|.
   - A) −7 | **B) 7** | C) 1 | D) −1
   - *First calculate inside: −3 + (−4) = −7. Then |−7| = 7.*

145. A lift starts at floor −2 (basement 2). It goes up 5 floors, then down 3 floors. What floor is it on?
   - **A) 0** | B) 2 | C) −1 | D) 4
   - *−2 + 5 = 3; 3 − 3 = 0. It is on floor 0 (ground floor).*

146. Calculate 1 − 2 + 3 − 4 + 5 − 6.
   - **A) −3** | B) 3 | C) 21 | D) −21
   - *Pair up: (1−2) + (3−4) + (5−6) = −1 + (−1) + (−1) = −3.*

147. If x = −3, evaluate x² − 2x + 1.
   - **A) 16** | B) 4 | C) 10 | D) 22
   - *(−3)² − 2(−3) + 1 = 9 + 6 + 1 = 16.*

148. Which is true about the number −√4?
   - A) It is irrational | **B) It equals −2 and is rational** | C) It equals 2 | D) It is undefined
   - *−√4 = −2. Since −2 is an integer, it is rational.*

149. Calculate −2 + 3 × (−4) − (−5).
   - **A) −9** | B) 9 | C) −15 | D) 15
   - *Multiply first: 3 × (−4) = −12. Then: −2 + (−12) − (−5) = −2 − 12 + 5 = −9.*

150. What type of number is 0?
   - A) Positive only | B) Negative only | **C) Neither positive nor negative** | D) Both positive and negative
   - *0 is neither positive nor negative. It is on the boundary between positives and negatives.*

### Additional

151. Calculate (−5)² − 5².
   - A) −50 | **B) 0** | C) 50 | D) 25
   - *(−5)² = 25 and 5² = 25. So 25 − 25 = 0.*

---

## Topic 3: Approximation & Estimation
*Rounding, significant figures, estimation* — 147 questions

1. How many significant figures are in 0.00350?
   - A) 2 | **B) 3** | C) 4 | D) 5
   - *Leading zeros aren't significant. Digits: 3, 5, and trailing 0 after decimal = 3 s.f.*

2. How many significant figures does 50.040 have?
   - A) 3 | B) 4 | **C) 5** | D) 2
   - *5, 0 (trapped), 0 (trapped), 4, 0 (trailing after decimal) = 5 s.f.*

3. How many significant figures are in 3,600?
   - **A) 2** | B) 3 | C) 4 | D) 1
   - *Trailing zeros in a whole number are not significant. Only 3 and 6 count = 2 s.f.*

4. How many significant figures does 10.00 have?
   - A) 1 | B) 2 | C) 3 | **D) 4**
   - *1, 0 (trapped), 0 (trailing after decimal), 0 (trailing after decimal) = 4 s.f.*

5. How many significant figures does 0.0600 have?
   - A) 1 | B) 2 | **C) 3** | D) 4
   - *Leading zeros not significant. 6, 0 (trailing), 0 (trailing) = 3 s.f.*

6. How many significant figures does 400.0 have?
   - A) 1 | B) 2 | C) 3 | **D) 4**
   - *4, 0 (trapped), 0 (trapped), 0 (trailing after decimal) = 4 s.f.*

7. How many significant figures are in 0.10200?
   - A) 3 | B) 4 | **C) 5** | D) 6
   - *Leading 0 not counted. 1, 0 (trapped), 2, 0 (trailing), 0 (trailing) = 5 s.f.*

8. A student records 3.450 m. How many significant figures?
   - A) 3 | **B) 4** | C) 2 | D) 5
   - *3, 4, 5, and trailing 0 after decimal = 4 s.f.*

9. How many significant figures does 1,000,000 have?
   - **A) 1** | B) 4 | C) 6 | D) 7
   - *Trailing zeros in a whole number aren't significant. Only the 1 counts = 1 s.f.*

10. How many significant figures does 0.007 have?
   - **A) 1** | B) 2 | C) 3 | D) 4
   - *Leading zeros are never significant. Only the 7 is significant = 1 s.f.*

11. How many significant figures are in 305?
   - A) 1 | B) 2 | **C) 3** | D) 4
   - *3 (non-zero), 0 (trapped between 3 and 5), 5 (non-zero) = 3 s.f.*

12. How many significant figures does 7.00 have?
   - A) 1 | B) 2 | **C) 3** | D) 4
   - *7 (non-zero), 0 (trailing after decimal), 0 (trailing after decimal) = 3 s.f.*

13. How many significant figures are in 90,500?
   - A) 2 | **B) 3** | C) 4 | D) 5
   - *9, 0 (trapped), 5 are significant. The trailing two zeros are not = 3 s.f.*

14. How many significant figures does 0.00100 have?
   - A) 1 | B) 2 | **C) 3** | D) 4
   - *Leading zeros not counted. 1, 0 (trailing), 0 (trailing) = 3 s.f.*

15. How many significant figures are in 1050?
   - A) 2 | **B) 3** | C) 4 | D) 5
   - *1 (non-zero), 0 (trapped), 5 (non-zero) = 3 s.f. The trailing zero is not significant.*

16. How many significant figures does 250.0 have?
   - A) 2 | B) 3 | **C) 4** | D) 5
   - *2, 5, 0 (the decimal point makes the trailing zero significant), 0 (trailing after decimal) = 4 s.f.*

17. How many significant figures are in 6.022 × 10³?
   - A) 1 | B) 2 | C) 3 | **D) 4**
   - *In scientific notation, all digits in the coefficient are significant: 6, 0, 2, 2 = 4 s.f.*

18. How many significant figures does 0.230 have?
   - A) 1 | B) 2 | **C) 3** | D) 4
   - *Leading 0 not counted. 2, 3, 0 (trailing after decimal) = 3 s.f.*

19. How many significant figures are in 45,000?
   - A) 1 | **B) 2** | C) 3 | D) 5
   - *4 and 5 are significant. Trailing zeros in a whole number are not = 2 s.f.*

20. How many significant figures does 0.0505 have?
   - A) 2 | **B) 3** | C) 4 | D) 5
   - *Leading zeros not significant. 5, 0 (trapped), 5 = 3 s.f.*

21. How many significant figures are in 8.060?
   - A) 2 | B) 3 | **C) 4** | D) 5
   - *8, 0 (trapped), 6, 0 (trailing after decimal) = 4 s.f.*

22. How many significant figures does 1200.0 have?
   - A) 2 | B) 3 | C) 4 | **D) 5**
   - *1, 2, 0 (trapped), 0 (trapped), 0 (trailing after decimal) = 5 s.f.*

23. How many significant figures are in 0.000902?
   - A) 1 | B) 2 | **C) 3** | D) 6
   - *Leading zeros not significant. 9, 0 (trapped), 2 = 3 s.f.*

24. How many significant figures does 30.00 have?
   - A) 1 | B) 2 | C) 3 | **D) 4**
   - *3, 0 (trapped by decimal), 0 (trailing), 0 (trailing) = 4 s.f.*

25. How many significant figures are in 500.?
   - A) 1 | B) 2 | **C) 3** | D) 4
   - *The decimal point after 500 means all three digits are significant: 5, 0, 0 = 3 s.f.*

26. How many significant figures does 0.01010 have?
   - A) 2 | B) 3 | **C) 4** | D) 5
   - *Leading zeros not counted. 1, 0 (trapped), 1, 0 (trailing) = 4 s.f.*

27. How many significant figures are in 7200?
   - A) 1 | **B) 2** | C) 3 | D) 4
   - *7 and 2 are significant; trailing zeros in a whole number are not = 2 s.f.*

28. How many significant figures does 9.0900 have?
   - A) 3 | B) 4 | **C) 5** | D) 6
   - *9, 0 (trapped), 9, 0 (trailing), 0 (trailing) = 5 s.f.*

29. How many significant figures are in 0.2050?
   - A) 2 | B) 3 | **C) 4** | D) 5
   - *Leading 0 not counted. 2, 0 (trapped), 5, 0 (trailing) = 4 s.f.*

30. How many significant figures does 6000.0 have?
   - A) 2 | B) 3 | C) 4 | **D) 5**
   - *6, 0 (trapped), 0 (trapped), 0 (trapped), 0 (trailing after decimal) = 5 s.f.*

31. Round 4.6729 to 3 s.f.
   - **A) 4.67** | B) 4.68 | C) 4.673 | D) 4.70
   - *3rd s.f. is 7. Next digit 2 < 5, round down → 4.67.*

32. Round 0.08547 to 2 s.f.
   - **A) 0.085** | B) 0.086 | C) 0.09 | D) 0.0855
   - *2 s.f.: 8, 5. Next digit 4 < 5, round down → 0.085.*

33. Round 12,465 to 3 s.f.
   - A) 12,400 | **B) 12,500** | C) 12,465 | D) 12,000
   - *3rd s.f. is 4. Next digit 6 ≥ 5, round up → 12,500.*

34. Round 0.009962 to 3 s.f.
   - A) 0.009 | **B) 0.00996** | C) 0.010 | D) 0.0100
   - *3 s.f.: 9, 9, 6. Next digit 2 < 5, round down → 0.00996.*

35. Round 99.96 to 3 s.f.
   - A) 99.9 | **B) 100** | C) 99.96 | D) 100.0
   - *3rd s.f. is second 9. Next digit 6 ≥ 5 → 99.9 rounds up to 100.*

36. Round 0.003456 to 2 s.f.
   - **A) 0.0035** | B) 0.0034 | C) 0.003 | D) 0.00346
   - *2 s.f.: 3, 4. Next digit 5 ≥ 5, round up → 0.0035.*

37. Round 0.06049 to 2 s.f.
   - **A) 0.060** | B) 0.061 | C) 0.06 | D) 0.062
   - *2 s.f.: 6, 0. Next digit 4 < 5, round down → 0.060.*

38. Round 874.6 to 2 s.f.
   - **A) 870** | B) 880 | C) 874 | D) 900
   - *2 s.f.: 8, 7. Next digit 4 < 5, round down → 870.*

39. Round 0.5555 to 3 s.f.
   - A) 0.555 | **B) 0.556** | C) 0.55 | D) 0.560
   - *3 s.f.: 5, 5, 5. Next digit 5 ≥ 5, round up → 0.556.*

40. Round 3.0049 to 3 s.f.
   - **A) 3.00** | B) 3.005 | C) 3.01 | D) 3.0
   - *3 s.f.: 3, 0, 0. Next digit 4 < 5, round down → 3.00.*

41. Round 29,851 to 2 s.f.
   - A) 29,000 | **B) 30,000** | C) 29,900 | D) 28,000
   - *2 s.f.: 2, 9. Next digit 8 ≥ 5, round up → 30,000.*

42. Round 0.004082 to 2 s.f.
   - A) 0.0040 | **B) 0.0041** | C) 0.004 | D) 0.00408
   - *2 s.f.: 4, 0. Next digit 8 ≥ 5, round up → 0.0041.*

43. Round 1.0045 to 4 s.f.
   - A) 1.004 | **B) 1.005** | C) 1.00 | D) 1.0045
   - *4 s.f.: 1, 0, 0, 4. Next digit 5 ≥ 5, round up → 1.005.*

44. Round 60,450 to 2 s.f.
   - **A) 60,000** | B) 61,000 | C) 60,500 | D) 60,400
   - *2 s.f.: 6, 0. Next digit 4 < 5, round down → 60,000.*

45. Round 0.19950 to 3 s.f.
   - A) 0.199 | **B) 0.200** | C) 0.20 | D) 0.1995
   - *3 s.f.: 1, 9, 9. Next digit 5 ≥ 5, round up → 0.200.*

46. Round 7,849 to 2 s.f.
   - **A) 7,800** | B) 7,900 | C) 7,850 | D) 8,000
   - *2 s.f.: 7, 8. Next digit 4 < 5, round down → 7,800.*

47. Round 0.002350 to 2 s.f.
   - A) 0.0023 | **B) 0.0024** | C) 0.002 | D) 0.00235
   - *2 s.f.: 2, 3. Next digit 5 ≥ 5, round up → 0.0024.*

48. Round 3.7284 to 3 s.f.
   - A) 3.72 | **B) 3.73** | C) 3.7 | D) 3.728
   - *3 s.f.: 3, 7, 2. Next digit 8 ≥ 5, round up → 3.73.*

49. Round 18,350 to 3 s.f.
   - A) 18,300 | **B) 18,400** | C) 18,350 | D) 18,000
   - *3 s.f.: 1, 8, 3. Next digit 5 ≥ 5, round up → 18,400.*

50. Round 0.07651 to 1 s.f.
   - A) 0.07 | **B) 0.08** | C) 0.1 | D) 0.076
   - *1 s.f. is 7. Next digit 6 ≥ 5, round up → 0.08.*

51. Round 456.7 to 2 s.f.
   - A) 450 | **B) 460** | C) 456 | D) 500
   - *2 s.f.: 4, 5. Next digit 6 ≥ 5, round up → 460.*

52. Round 0.0009995 to 3 s.f.
   - A) 0.000999 | **B) 0.00100** | C) 0.001 | D) 0.0010
   - *3 s.f.: 9, 9, 9. Next digit 5 ≥ 5 → 0.00100.*

53. Round 23.449 to 3 s.f.
   - **A) 23.4** | B) 23.5 | C) 23.449 | D) 23.44
   - *3 s.f.: 2, 3, 4. Next digit 4 < 5, round down → 23.4.*

54. Round 1,055 to 2 s.f.
   - A) 1,000 | **B) 1,100** | C) 1,050 | D) 1,060
   - *2 s.f.: 1, 0. Next digit 5 ≥ 5, round up → 1,100.*

55. Round 0.040601 to 3 s.f.
   - **A) 0.0406** | B) 0.0407 | C) 0.041 | D) 0.040
   - *3 s.f.: 4, 0, 6. Next digit 0 < 5, round down → 0.0406.*

56. Round 8,500 to 1 s.f.
   - A) 8,000 | **B) 9,000** | C) 8,500 | D) 10,000
   - *1 s.f. is 8. Next digit 5 ≥ 5, round up → 9,000.*

57. Round 0.3049 to 2 s.f.
   - **A) 0.30** | B) 0.31 | C) 0.3 | D) 0.304
   - *2 s.f.: 3, 0. Next digit 4 < 5, round down → 0.30.*

58. Round 199.5 to 3 s.f.
   - A) 199 | **B) 200** | C) 199.5 | D) 200.
   - *3 s.f.: 1, 9, 9. Next digit 5 ≥ 5, round up → 200.*

59. Round 6.0050 to 3 s.f.
   - A) 6.00 | **B) 6.01** | C) 6.005 | D) 6.0
   - *3 s.f.: 6, 0, 0. Next digit 5 ≥ 5, round up → 6.01.*

60. Round 4,444 to 1 s.f.
   - **A) 4,000** | B) 5,000 | C) 4,400 | D) 4,440
   - *1 s.f. is 4. Next digit 4 < 5, round down → 4,000.*

61. Round 3.14159 to 2 d.p.
   - **A) 3.14** | B) 3.15 | C) 3.1 | D) 3.142
   - *2 d.p.: 3.14. Next digit 1 < 5, round down → 3.14.*

   - A) 6.2 | **B) 6.3** | C) 6.28 | D) 6.27
   - *1 d.p.: 6.2. Next digit 7 ≥ 5, round up → 6.3.*

   - A) 0.045 | **B) 0.046** | C) 0.0456 | D) 0.04562
   - *3 d.p.: 0.045. Next digit 6 ≥ 5, round up → 0.046.*

   - A) 12.34 | **B) 12.35** | C) 12.3 | D) 12.346
   - *2 d.p.: 12.34. Next digit 5 ≥ 5, round up → 12.35.*

   - A) 0.666 | **B) 0.667** | C) 0.66 | D) 0.6666

   - A) 100.00 | **B) 100.01** | C) 100.0 | D) 100.005

   - **A) 267.4** | B) 267.5 | C) 267.44 | D) 267.45
   - *1 d.p.: 267.4. Next digit 4 < 5, round down → 267.4.*

   - A) 0.09 | **B) 0.10** | C) 0.099 | D) 0.100

   - **A) 18** | B) 15 | C) 20 | D) 12
   - *600 × 0.03 = 18.*

83. Estimate (78.3 + 21.9) ÷ 0.48 using 1 s.f.
   - A) 100 | **B) 200** | C) 250 | D) 150
   - *80 + 20 = 100; 100 ÷ 0.5 = 200.*

84. Estimate 0.00712 × 4800 using 1 s.f.
   - A) 24 | **B) 35** | C) 40 | D) 30
   - *0.007 × 5000 = 35.*

85. Estimate 312 ÷ 0.0049 using 1 s.f.
   - **A) 60,000** | B) 6,000 | C) 600 | D) 600,000
   - *300 ÷ 0.005 = 60,000.*

86. Estimate 387 × 0.0214 using 1 s.f.
   - A) 4 | **B) 8** | C) 16 | D) 2
   - *400 × 0.02 = 8.*

87. Estimate 725 ÷ 8.3 using 1 s.f.
   - A) 70 | B) 80 | **C) 90** | D) 100
   - *700 ÷ 8 ≈ 87.5 ≈ 90.*

88. Estimate 0.0049 × 1,960 using 1 s.f.
   - A) 8 | **B) 10** | C) 12 | D) 5
   - *0.005 × 2000 = 10.*

   - **A) 3** | B) 3.5 | C) 4 | D) 6
   - *600 × 0.005 = 3.*

90. Estimate (499 + 312) ÷ 0.097 using 1 s.f.
   - A) 4,000 | **B) 8,000** | C) 10,000 | D) 5,000
   - *500 + 300 = 800; 800 ÷ 0.1 = 8,000.*

91. Estimate 0.00183 × 5,200 using 1 s.f.
   - A) 5 | **B) 10** | C) 15 | D) 1
   - *0.002 × 5000 = 10.*

92. Estimate 8,920 ÷ 0.044 using 1 s.f.
   - A) 20,000 | **B) 200,000** | C) 2,000 | D) 2,000,000
   - *9000 ÷ 0.04 = 9000 × 25 = 225,000 ≈ 200,000.*

   - **A) 0.024** | B) 0.24 | C) 2.4 | D) 0.0024

   - *20 × 3 = 60.*

95. Estimate 4,780 ÷ 0.52 using 1 s.f.

   - *(0.03 + 0.07) = 0.1; 0.1 × 50 = 5.*

108. Which of these has 4 significant figures?
   - A) 3,700 | B) 0.0370 | **C) 37.00** | D) 370
   - *37.00 has 4 s.f.: 3, 7, 0 (trailing after decimal), 0 (trailing). The others each have 2 or 3.*

109. Which number is rounded to 3 s.f.?
   - A) 0.04560 | **B) 0.0456** | C) 0.04 | D) 0.046
   - *0.0456 has exactly 3 s.f. (4, 5, 6). Leading zeros don't count.*

110. A bag weighs 1.275 kg. What is this to 3 s.f.?
   - A) 1.27 kg | **B) 1.28 kg** | C) 1.3 kg | D) 1.275 kg
   - *3 s.f.: 1, 2, 7. Next digit 5 ≥ 5 → round up → 1.28 kg.*

111. A race is 100.48 m. Round to 4 s.f.
   - A) 100.4 m | **B) 100.5 m** | C) 100.48 m | D) 100.0 m

112. Which of these equals 0.003050 rounded to 2 s.f.?
   - **A) 0.0031** | B) 0.0030 | C) 0.003 | D) 0.00305
   - *2 s.f.: 3, 0. Next digit is 5 ≥ 5, round up → 0.0031.*

113. A scientist writes 2.40 × 10⁻³. How many s.f.?
   - A) 1 | B) 2 | **C) 3** | D) 4
   - *In scientific notation all digits in 2.40 are significant: 2, 4, 0 = 3 s.f.*

114. Round 0.004550 to 2 s.f.
   - A) 0.0045 | **B) 0.0046** | C) 0.005 | D) 0.00455
   - *2 s.f.: 4, 5. Next digit 5 ≥ 5, round up → 0.0046.*

115. A plank is 2.745 m. Round to 3 s.f.
   - A) 2.74 m | **B) 2.75 m** | C) 2.7 m | D) 2.745 m
   - *3 s.f.: 2, 7, 4. Next digit 5 ≥ 5 → 2.75 m.*

116. How many s.f. in 0.00040050?
   - A) 3 | B) 4 | **C) 5** | D) 7
   - *Leading zeros not significant. 4, 0 (trapped), 0 (trapped), 5, 0 (trailing) = 5 s.f.*

117. Round 0.9999 to 2 s.f.
   - A) 0.99 | **B) 1.0** | C) 1.00 | D) 0.999
   - *2 s.f.: 9, 9. Next digit 9 ≥ 5 → 0.99 rounds up → 1.0.*

118. Estimate (4.98²) using 1 s.f.
   - A) 20 | **B) 25** | C) 30 | D) 15
   - *5² = 25.*

119. Round 0.1005 to 3 s.f.
   - A) 0.100 | **B) 0.101** | C) 0.10 | D) 0.1005
   - *3 s.f.: 1, 0, 0. Next digit is 5 ≥ 5, round up → 0.101.*

120. A bottle holds 0.4750 L. How many s.f.?
   - A) 2 | B) 3 | **C) 4** | D) 5
   - *4, 7, 5, 0 (trailing after decimal) = 4 s.f.*

121. Round 0.6050 to 2 s.f.
   - A) 0.60 | **B) 0.61** | C) 0.6 | D) 0.605
   - *2 s.f.: 6, 0. Next digit 5 ≥ 5 → round up → 0.61.*

122. Which answer shows 56,789 rounded to 3 s.f.?
   - A) 56,700 | **B) 56,800** | C) 56,790 | D) 57,000
   - *3 s.f.: 5, 6, 7. Next digit 8 ≥ 5 → 56,800.*

123. How many s.f. in 10,010?
   - A) 2 | B) 3 | **C) 4** | D) 5
   - *1, 0 (trapped), 0 (trapped), 1, 0... The trailing zero is not significant = 4 s.f.*

124. Estimate √(0.0396) using 1 s.f.
   - A) 0.06 | **B) 0.2** | C) 0.02 | D) 2
   - *0.04 ≈ 4/100; √(4/100) = 2/10 = 0.2.*

125. Round 0.009090 to 2 s.f.
   - A) 0.0090 | **B) 0.0091** | C) 0.009 | D) 0.00909
   - *2 s.f.: 9, 0. Next digit is 9 ≥ 5, round up → 0.0091.*

126. Which shows 2,350 rounded to 2 s.f.?
   - A) 2,300 | **B) 2,400** | C) 2,350 | D) 2,000
   - *2 s.f.: 2, 3. Next digit 5 ≥ 5 → 2,400.*

127. How many s.f. does 3.0 × 10⁴ have?
   - A) 1 | **B) 2** | C) 3 | D) 4
   - *3.0 in the coefficient has 2 s.f. (3 and the trailing zero after the decimal).*

128. A runner clocks 9.580 s. How many s.f.?
   - A) 2 | B) 3 | **C) 4** | D) 5
   - *9, 5, 8, 0 (trailing after decimal) = 4 s.f.*

129. Round 0.0002049 to 2 s.f.
   - **A) 0.00020** | B) 0.00021 | C) 0.0002 | D) 0.000205
   - *2 s.f.: 2, 0. Next digit 4 < 5 → 0.00020.*

130. Estimate 0.00489 ÷ 0.00102 using 1 s.f.
   - A) 4 | **B) 5** | C) 6 | D) 0.5
   - *0.005 ÷ 0.001 = 5.*

131. Round 7.0050 to 4 s.f.
   - **A) 7.005** | B) 7.004 | C) 7.006 | D) 7.00
   - *4 s.f.: 7, 0, 0, 5. Next digit 0 < 5 → 7.005.*

132. Which has exactly 2 s.f.?
   - A) 30.0 | **B) 0.030** | C) 3,000 | D) 30
   - *0.030: leading 0 not significant; 3, 0 (trailing) = 2 s.f. ✓*

133. Estimate 0.00052 × 38,000 using 1 s.f.
   - **A) 20** | B) 2 | C) 200 | D) 0.2
   - *0.0005 × 40,000 = 20.*

134. Round 1.0995 to 3 s.f.
   - A) 1.09 | **B) 1.10** | C) 1.099 | D) 1.1
   - *3 s.f.: 1, 0, 9. Next digit 9 ≥ 5 → round up: 1.10.*

135. How many s.f. in 4.000 × 10²?
   - A) 1 | B) 2 | C) 3 | **D) 4**
   - *4.000 has 4 s.f. (4, and three trailing zeros after the decimal).*

136. Round 0.050505 to 3 s.f.
   - **A) 0.0505** | B) 0.0506 | C) 0.051 | D) 0.05050
   - *3 s.f.: 5, 0, 5. Next digit 0 < 5 → 0.0505.*

137. A wire measures 24.65 cm. Round to 3 s.f.
   - A) 24.6 cm | **B) 24.7 cm** | C) 24.65 cm | D) 25.0 cm
   - *3 s.f.: 2, 4, 6. Next digit 5 ≥ 5 → 24.7 cm.*

138. Which of these numbers has exactly 3 s.f.?
   - A) 0.0030 | B) 4,500 | C) 8.010 | **D) 0.310**
   - *0.310: 3, 1, 0 (trailing after decimal) = 3 s.f. ✓*

139. Round 0.001505 to 3 s.f.
   - A) 0.00150 | **B) 0.00151** | C) 0.0015 | D) 0.001505

140. A thermometer reads 36.850°C. Round to 4 s.f.

141. How many s.f. in 0.090090?
   - A) 3 | B) 4 | **C) 5** | D) 6
   - *Leading zeros not significant. 9, 0 (trapped), 0 (trapped), 9, 0 (trailing) = 5 s.f.*

142. Round 49,950 to 3 s.f.
   - A) 49,900 | **B) 50,000** | C) 49,950 | D) 49,000

144. A brick is 0.2405 m long. Round to 2 s.f.

145. How many s.f. does 80,080 have?
   - A) 2 | B) 3 | **C) 4** | D) 5
   - *8, 0 (trapped), 0 (trapped), 8 = 4 s.f. The final zero is trailing in a whole number and not significant.*

146. Round 0.050950 to 3 s.f.
   - A) 0.0509 | **B) 0.0510** | C) 0.051 | D) 0.05095
   - *3 s.f.: 5, 0, 9. Next digit 5 ≥ 5, round up → 0.0510.*

147. Which value is 0.006241 rounded to 2 s.f.?

   - *2 s.f.: 6, 2. Next digit 4 < 5, round down → 0.0062.*
